data-height=&quot;240&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;328800&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97002997003&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8c/F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv/F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv.360p.vp9.webm&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;VP9 (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;VP9 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.vp9.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;640&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;557232&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97002997003&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8c/F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv/F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv.360p.webm&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;WebM (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;WebM 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;640&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;575704&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97002997003&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:F-18 - A 3-wire landing.ogv" style="width:220px;height:124px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv/220px--F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:F-18_-_A_3-wire_landing.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>F/A-18 Hornet aircraft landing video</div></div></div>\n<p>Carriers steam at speed, up to 35 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knots</a> (65&#160;km/h; 40&#160;mph) into the wind during flight deck operations to increase wind speed over the deck to a safe minimum. This increase in effective wind speed provides a higher launch airspeed for aircraft at the end of the catapult stroke or ski-jump, as well as making recovery safer by reducing the difference between the relative speeds of the aircraft and ship.\n</p><p>Since the early 1950s on conventional carriers it has been the practice to recover aircraft at an angle to port of the axial line of the ship. The primary function of this angled deck is to allow aircraft that miss the arresting wires, referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Bolter_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolter (aviation)">bolter</a>, to become airborne again without the risk of hitting aircraft parked forward. The angled deck allows the installation of one or two "waist" catapults in addition to the two bow cats. An angled deck also improves <a href="/wiki/Launch_and_recovery_cycle" title="Launch and recovery cycle">launch and recovery cycle</a> flexibility with the option of simultaneous launching and recovery of aircraft.\n</p><p>Conventional ("tailhook") aircraft rely upon a <a href="/wiki/Landing_Signal_Officer" title="Landing Signal Officer">landing signal officer</a> (LSO, radio call sign <i>paddles</i>) to monitor the aircraft\'s approach, visually gauge glideslope, attitude, and airspeed, and transmit that data to the pilot. Before the angled deck emerged in the 1950s, LSOs used colored paddles to signal corrections to the pilot (hence the nickname). From the late 1950s onward, visual landing aids such as the <a href="/wiki/Optical_landing_system" title="Optical landing system">optical landing system</a> have provided information on proper <a href="/wiki/Glide_slope" class="mw-redirect" title="Glide slope">glide slope</a>, but LSOs still transmit voice calls to approaching pilots by radio.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Harry_S_Truman_(CVN-75)_Flight_Deck.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/USS_Harry_S_Truman_%28CVN-75%29_Flight_Deck.JPG/220px-USS_Harry_S_Truman_%28CVN-75%29_Flight_Deck.JPG" width="220" height="92" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/USS_Harry_S_Truman_%28CVN-75%29_Flight_Deck.JPG/330px-USS_Harry_S_Truman_%28CVN-75%29_Flight_Deck.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/USS_Harry_S_Truman_%28CVN-75%29_Flight_Deck.JPG/440px-USS_Harry_S_Truman_%28CVN-75%29_Flight_Deck.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1977" data-file-height="823" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Harry_S_Truman_(CVN-75)_Flight_Deck.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/F/A-18_Hornet" class="mw-redirect" title="F/A-18 Hornet">F/A-18 Hornets</a> on the flight deck of the <a href="/wiki/Nimitz-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Nimitz-class aircraft carrier"><i>Nimitz</i>-class</a> carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_Harry_S._Truman_(CVN-75)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Harry S. Truman (CVN-75)"><i>Harry S. Truman</i></a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg/220px-USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg/330px-USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg/440px-USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1802" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_John_C._Stennis_flight_operations_121229-N-OY799-239.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/USS_John_C._Stennis" title="USS John C. Stennis">USS&#160;<i>John C. Stennis</i></a> shooter launching F/A-18</div></div></div>\n<p>Key personnel involved in the flight deck include the shooters, the handler, and the air boss. Shooters are <a href="/wiki/Naval_aviator" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval aviator">naval aviators</a> or <a href="/wiki/Naval_flight_officer" title="Naval flight officer">naval flight officers</a> and are responsible for launching aircraft. The handler works just inside the island from the flight deck and is responsible for the movement of aircraft before launching and after recovery. The "air boss" (usually a <a href="/wiki/Commander" title="Commander">commander</a>) occupies the top bridge (Primary Flight Control, also called <i>primary</i> or <i>the tower</i>) and has the overall responsibility for controlling launch, recovery and "those aircraft in the air near the ship, and the movement of planes on the flight deck, which itself resembles a well-choreographed ballet."<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The captain of the ship spends most of his time one level below primary on the Navigation Bridge. Below this is the Flag Bridge, designated for the embarked admiral and his staff.\n</p><p>To facilitate working on the flight deck of a U.S. aircraft carrier, the sailors wear colored shirts that designate their responsibilities. There are at least seven different colors worn by flight deck personnel for <a href="/wiki/Modern_United_States_Navy_carrier_air_operations" title="Modern United States Navy carrier air operations">modern United States Navy carrier air operations</a>. Carrier operations of other nations use similar color schemes.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deck_structures">Deck structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Deck structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100512-N-8446A-004_An_F-A-18F_Super_Hornet_assigned_to_the_Fighting_Checkmates_of_Strike_Fighter_Squadron_(VFA)_211_lands_aboard_the_aircraft_carrier_USS_Enterprise_(CVN_65).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/US_Navy_100512-N-8446A-004_An_F-A-18F_Super_Hornet_assigned_to_the_Fighting_Checkmates_of_Strike_Fighter_Squadron_%28VFA%29_211_lands_aboard_the_aircraft_carrier_USS_Enterprise_%28CVN_65%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/US_Navy_100512-N-8446A-004_An_F-A-18F_Super_Hornet_assigned_to_the_Fighting_Checkmates_of_Strike_Fighter_Squadron_%28VFA%29_211_lands_aboard_the_aircraft_carrier_USS_Enterprise_%28CVN_65%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/US_Navy_100512-N-8446A-004_An_F-A-18F_Super_Hornet_assigned_to_the_Fighting_Checkmates_of_Strike_Fighter_Squadron_%28VFA%29_211_lands_aboard_the_aircraft_carrier_USS_Enterprise_%28CVN_65%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100512-N-8446A-004_An_F-A-18F_Super_Hornet_assigned_to_the_Fighting_Checkmates_of_Strike_Fighter_Squadron_(VFA)_211_lands_aboard_the_aircraft_carrier_USS_Enterprise_(CVN_65).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Island control structure of <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(CVN-65)" title="USS Enterprise (CVN-65)">USS&#160;<i>Enterprise</i></a></div></div></div>\n<p>The superstructure of a carrier (such as the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridge (ship)">bridge</a>, flight <a href="/wiki/Control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Control tower">control tower</a>) are concentrated in a relatively small area called an <i>island</i>, a feature pioneered on <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hermes_(95)" title="HMS Hermes (95)">HMS&#160;<i>Hermes</i></a> in 1923. While the island is usually built on the <a href="/wiki/Starboard" class="mw-redirect" title="Starboard">starboard</a> side of the flight deck, the Japanese aircraft carriers <a href="/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Akagi" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Akagi"><i>Akagi</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Hiry%C5%AB" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Hiry\xc5\xab"><i>Hiry\xc5\xab</i></a> had their islands built on the <a href="/wiki/Port_and_starboard" title="Port and starboard">port</a> side. Very few carriers have been designed or built without an island. The <i>flush deck</i> configuration proved to have significant drawbacks, primary of which was management of the exhaust from the power plant. Fumes coming across the deck were a major issue in <a href="/wiki/USS_Langley_(CV-1)" title="USS Langley (CV-1)">USS&#160;<i>Langley</i></a>. In addition, lack of an island meant difficulties managing the flight deck, performing air traffic control, a lack of radar housing placements and problems with navigating and controlling the ship itself.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1983241\xe2\x80\x93243_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1983241\xe2\x80\x93243-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another deck structure that can be seen is a <a href="/wiki/Ski-jump_ramp" class="mw-redirect" title="Ski-jump ramp">ski-jump ramp</a> at the forward end of the flight deck. This was first developed to help launch <a href="/wiki/STOVL" title="STOVL">STOVL</a> aircraft take off at far higher weights than is possible with a vertical or rolling takeoff on flat decks. Originally developed by the Royal Navy, it since has been adopted by many navies for smaller carriers. A ski-jump ramp works by converting some of the forward rolling movement of the aircraft into vertical velocity and is sometimes combined with the aiming of jet thrust partly downwards. This allows heavily loaded and fueled aircraft a few more precious seconds to attain sufficient air velocity and lift to sustain normal flight. Without a ski-jump launching fully loaded and fueled aircraft such as the Harrier would not be possible on a smaller flat deck ship before either <a href="/wiki/Stall_(flight)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stall (flight)">stalling out</a> or crashing directly into the sea.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG/220px-FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG/330px-FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG/440px-FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="2640" data-file-height="1754" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FRS.1_ski-jump_take-off_HMS_Invincible.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ski-jump on Royal Navy carrier <a href="/wiki/HMS_Invincible_(R05)" title="HMS Invincible (R05)">HMS&#160;<i>Invincible</i></a></div></div></div>\n<p>Although STOVL aircraft are capable of taking off vertically from a spot on the deck, using the ramp and a running start is far more fuel efficient and permits a heavier launch weight. As catapults are unnecessary, carriers with this arrangement reduce weight, complexity, and space needed for complex steam or electromagnetic launching equipment, vertical landing aircraft also remove the need for arresting cables and related hardware. Russian, Chinese, and future Indian carriers include a ski-jump ramp for launching lightly loaded conventional fighter aircraft but recover using traditional carrier arresting cables and a tailhook on their aircraft.\n</p><p>The disadvantage of the ski-jump is the penalty it exacts on aircraft size, payload, and fuel load (and thus range); heavily laden aircraft can not launch using a ski-jump because their high loaded weight requires either a longer takeoff roll than is possible on a carrier deck, or assistance from a catapult or JATO rocket. For example, the Russian Su-33 is only able to launch from the carrier <a href="/wiki/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Admiral_Kuznetsov" title="Russian aircraft carrier Admiral Kuznetsov"><i>Admiral Kuznetsov</i></a> with a minimal armament and fuel load. Another disadvantage is on mixed flight deck operations where helicopters are also present such as a US <a href="/wiki/Landing_helicopter_dock" title="Landing helicopter dock">landing helicopter dock</a> or <a href="/wiki/Landing_helicopter_assault" class="mw-redirect" title="Landing helicopter assault">landing helicopter assault</a> amphibious assault ship a ski jump is not included as this would eliminate one or more helicopter landing areas, this flat deck limits the loading of Harriers but is somewhat mitigated by the longer rolling start provided by a long flight deck compared to many STOVL carriers.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_fleets">National fleets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: National fleets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg/280px-World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg.png" width="280" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg/420px-World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg/560px-World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="975" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Navy_Aircraft_carries_chart.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chart comparing a range of aircraft and helicopter carriers, in order of longest (top left) to shortest (bottom right)</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_aircraft_carriers_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="List of aircraft carriers by country">List of aircraft carriers by country</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_aircraft_carriers_in_service" title="List of aircraft carriers in service">List of aircraft carriers in service</a></div>\n<p>The U.S. Navy has the largest carriers in the world, and currently has eleven in service. The UK operates one 65,000 tonne STOVL carrier. The navies of China, France, India, and Russia each operate a single medium-sized fleet carrier. The US has nine similarly sized Amphibious Warfare Ships. There are three small light carriers in use capable of operating both fixed-wing aircraft and helicopters, Italy operates two, and Spain one.\n</p><p>Additionally there are fourteen small carriers which only operate helicopters serving the navies of Australia (2), Brazil (1), Egypt (2), France (3), Japan (4), South Korea (1), and Thailand (1).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMAS_Canberra_(LHD_02)_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/HMAS_Canberra_%28LHD_02%29_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg/220px-HMAS_Canberra_%28LHD_02%29_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/HMAS_Canberra_%28LHD_02%29_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg/330px-HMAS_Canberra_%28LHD_02%29_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/HMAS_Canberra_%28LHD_02%29_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg/440px-HMAS_Canberra_%28LHD_02%29_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2737" data-file-height="1827" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMAS_Canberra_(LHD_02)_at_berth_prior_to_commissioning.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMAS_Canberra_(L02)" title="HMAS Canberra (L02)">HMAS&#160;<i>Canberra</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Canberra-class_landing_helicopter_dock" title="Canberra-class landing helicopter dock"><i>Canberra</i>-class&#x20;landing helicopter dock</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canberra-class_landing_helicopter_dock" title="Canberra-class landing helicopter dock"><i>Canberra</i>&#x20;class</a> of landing helicopter docks is based on the Spanish vessel <a href="/wiki/Spanish_ship_Juan_Carlos_I_(L61)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish ship Juan Carlos I (L61)"><i>Juan Carlos I</i></a>. The two ship class, built by <a href="/wiki/Navantia" title="Navantia">Navantia</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Australia" title="BAE Systems Australia">BAE Systems Australia</a>, represents the largest ships ever built for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Naval-technology.com_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naval-technology.com-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/HMAS_Canberra_(L02)" title="HMAS Canberra (L02)">HMAS&#160;<i>Canberra</i></a> underwent sea trials in late 2013 and was commissioned in 2014. Her <a href="/wiki/Sister_ship" title="Sister ship">sister ship</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMAS_Adelaide_(L01)" title="HMAS Adelaide (L01)">HMAS&#160;<i>Adelaide</i></a>, was commissioned in December 2015. The Australian ships retain the ski-ramp from the <i>Juan Carlos I</i> design, although the RAN has not acquired carrier-based fixed-wing aircraft.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg/220px-HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg/330px-HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg/440px-HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1597" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Ocean_MOD_45151277.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)"><i>Atl\xc3\xa2ntico</i></a>, an <i>Ocean</i>-class multi-purpose <a href="/wiki/Helicopter_carrier" title="Helicopter carrier">helicopter carrier</a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_2">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Navy" title="Brazilian Navy">Brazilian Navy</a> commissioned the multi-purpose amphibious assault ship and helicopter carrier <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">HMS&#160;<i>Ocean</i></a> on 29 June in the United Kingdom, which was renamed <i>Atl\xc3\xa2ntico</i>. The helicopter carrier package for Brazil includes an Artisan 3D search radar, KH1007 surface surveillance radar system, four 30 mm DS30M Mk 2 remote weapon systems and four Mk 5B landing craft. However, the three original 20 mm Mk 15 Block 1B Phalanx close-in weapon systems, the torpedo defence systems and 7.62 mm M134 machine guns were removed from the ship before its transfer to Brazil.\nThe ship displaces 21.578 tonnes, is 203.43 m long and has a range of 8,000 n miles. She has been undergoing maintenance work by Babcock and BAE Systems since February.\nScheduled to reach its homeport, Arsenal do Rio de Janeiro (AMRJ), on 25 August, <i>Atl\xc3\xa2ntico</i> will undergo operational sea training under the Royal Navy\xe2\x80\x99s Flag Officer Sea Training (FOST) programme.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was reported in 2017 that Brazil was interested in purchasing <i>Ocean</i> from the UK as a replacement for <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_aircraft_carrier_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(A12)" title="Brazilian aircraft carrier S\xc3\xa3o Paulo (A12)"><i>S\xc3\xa3o Paulo</i></a> which was withdrawn from service in 2017 following multiple mechanical failures. The Royal Navy released an asking price of \xc2\xa380.3&#160;million (US$105,800,871), which the Brazilian Navy called "convenient".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>  In December 2017, the Brazilian Navy confirmed the purchase of <i>Ocean</i> for (GBP) \xc2\xa384.6&#160;million (equivalent to R$359.5M and US$113.2M). The ship was decommissioned from Royal Navy service in March 2018, and after undertaking a period of maintenance in the United Kingdom, is expected to arrive in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> by the end of 2018 with the intention of being fully operational by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg/220px-Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg/330px-Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg/440px-Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aircraft_Carrier_Liaoning_CV-16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chinese_aircraft_carrier_Liaoning" title="Chinese aircraft carrier Liaoning"><i>Liaoning</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Kuznetsov-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Kuznetsov-class aircraft carrier">Type 001 aircraft carrier</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_3">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>One <a href="/wiki/STOBAR" title="STOBAR">STOBAR</a> carrier: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_aircraft_carrier_Liaoning" title="Chinese aircraft carrier Liaoning"><i>Liaoning</i></a> was originally built as the 57,000 tonne Soviet <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Kuznetsov-class_aircraft_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiral Kuznetsov-class aircraft carrier"><i>Admiral Kuznetsov</i>-class</a> carrier <a href="/wiki/Kuznetsov-class_aircraft_carrier#Hull_2_-_Liaoning" title="Kuznetsov-class aircraft carrier"><i>Varyag</i></a><sup id="cite_ref-bbc20110608_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20110608-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and was later purchased as a stripped <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hulk (ship)">hulk</a> by China in 1998 on the pretext of use as a floating casino, then partially rebuilt and towed to China for completion.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> <i>Liaoning</i> was commissioned on 25 September 2012, and began service for testing and training.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On 24 or 25 November 2012, <i>Liaoning</i> successfully launched and recovered several <a href="/wiki/Shenyang_J-15" title="Shenyang J-15">Shenyang J-15</a> jet fighter aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> She is classified as a training ship, intended to allow the navy to practice with carrier usage. On 26 December 2012, the People\'s Daily reported that it will take four to five years for <i>Liaoning</i> to reach full capacity, mainly due to training and coordination which will take significant amount of time for Chinese <a href="/wiki/PLA_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="PLA Navy">PLA Navy</a> to complete as this is the first aircraft carrier in their possession.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> As she is a training ship, <i>Liaoning</i> is not assigned to any of China\'s operation fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A second carrier was launched on 26 April 2017. She is the first to be built domestically, to a modified <i>Kuznetsov</i>-class design. The <a href="/wiki/Type_001A_aircraft_carrier" title="Type 001A aircraft carrier">Type 001A aircraft carrier</a> started sea trials on 23 April 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-scmp_4/18_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmp_4/18-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and is scheduled to enter service in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Chinese officials stated that a third carrier, also known as <a href="/wiki/Chinese_aircraft_carrier_programme#Type_002" title="Chinese aircraft carrier programme">Type 002 carrier</a> is being constructed in the Shanghai Jiangnan Shipyard. She will be the first Chinese aircraft carrier to use catapult take off system.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg/220px-ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg/330px-ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg/440px-ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ENS_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_LHD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Egyptian_ship_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian ship Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a></i> LHD docked at <a href="/wiki/Saint-Nazaire" title="Saint-Nazaire">Saint-Nazaire</a>, April 2016</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_4">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Egypt signed a contract with French shipbuilder <a href="/wiki/DCNS_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="DCNS (company)">DCNS</a> to buy two <a href="/wiki/Mistral-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="Mistral-class amphibious assault ship"><i>Mistral</i>-class</a> helicopter carriers for approximately 950 million euros. The two ships were originally destined for Russia, but the deal was canceled by France due to Russian involvement in Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 2 June 2016, Egypt received the first of two helicopter carriers acquired in October 2015, the landing helicopter dock <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_ship_Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian ship Gamal Abdel Nasser"><i>Gamal Abdel Nasser</i></a>. The flag transfer ceremony took place in the presence of Egyptian and French Navies\xe2\x80\x99 chiefs of staff, chairman and chief executive officers of both DCNS and STX France, and senior Egyptian and French officials.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On 16 September 2016, DCNS delivered the second of two helicopter carriers, the landing helicopter dock <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_ship_Anwar_El_Sadat" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian ship Anwar El Sadat"><i>Anwar El Sadat</i></a> which also participated in a joint exercise with the French Navy before arriving at its home port of Alexandria.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Egypt is the first and so far only country in Africa or the Middle East to possess an aircraft carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_De_Gaulle_(R91)_underway_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Charles_De_Gaulle_%28R91%29_underway_2009.jpg/220px-Charles_De_Gaulle_%28R91%29_underway_2009.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Charles_De_Gaulle_%28R91%29_underway_2009.jpg/330px-Charles_De_Gaulle_%28R91%29_underway_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Charles_De_Gaulle_%28R91%29_underway_2009.jpg/440px-Charles_De_Gaulle_%28R91%29_underway_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="570" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_De_Gaulle_(R91)_underway_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/French_aircraft_carrier_Charles_de_Gaulle_(R91)" class="mw-redirect" title="French aircraft carrier Charles de Gaulle (R91)"><i>Charles de Gaulle</i></a> of the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_5">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>1 <a href="/wiki/CATOBAR" title="CATOBAR">CATOBAR</a> carrier: <a href="/wiki/French_aircraft_carrier_Charles_de_Gaulle_(R91)" class="mw-redirect" title="French aircraft carrier Charles de Gaulle (R91)"><i>Charles de Gaulle</i></a> is a 42,000 tonne nuclear-powered aircraft carrier, commissioned in 2001 and is the flagship of the French Navy (Marine Nationale). The ship carries a complement of <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Rafale" title="Dassault Rafale">Dassault Rafale&#160;M</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grumman_E-2_Hawkeye" class="mw-redirect" title="Grumman E-2 Hawkeye">E\xe2\x80\x912C Hawkeye</a> aircraft, <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_EC725" title="Eurocopter EC725">EC725 Caracal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_AS532_Cougar" title="Eurocopter AS532 Cougar">AS532 Cougar</a> helicopters for <a href="/wiki/Combat_search_and_rescue" title="Combat search and rescue">combat search and rescue</a>, as well as modern electronics and <a href="/wiki/MBDA_Aster" class="mw-redirect" title="MBDA Aster">Aster</a> missiles. She is a <a href="/wiki/CATOBAR" title="CATOBAR">CATOBAR</a>-type carrier that uses two 75&#160;m C13\xe2\x80\x913 steam catapults of a shorter version of the catapult system installed on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Nimitz-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Nimitz-class aircraft carrier"><i>Nimitz</i>-class</a> carriers, one catapult at the bow and one across the front of the landing area.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>3 amphibious assault ships: <a href="/wiki/Mistral-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="Mistral-class amphibious assault ship"><i>Mistral</i>&#x20;class</a>, 21,500 tonne full deck amphibious assault ships with hospital and well deck.<sup id="cite_ref-Mistral_Class_\xe2\x80\x93_Amphibious_Assault_Ships_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mistral_Class_\xe2\x80\x93_Amphibious_Assault_Ships-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg/220px-INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg/330px-INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg/440px-INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="998" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:INS_Vikramaditya_13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indian Navy\'s aircraft carriers <a href="/wiki/INS_Vikramaditya_(R33)" class="mw-redirect" title="INS Vikramaditya (R33)">INS&#160;<i>Vikramaditya</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/INS_Viraat_(R22)" class="mw-redirect" title="INS Viraat (R22)">INS&#160;<i>Viraat</i></a> in 2014</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_6">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>1 <a href="/wiki/STOBAR" title="STOBAR">STOBAR</a> carrier: <a href="/wiki/INS_Vikramaditya" title="INS Vikramaditya">INS&#160;<i>Vikramaditya</i></a>, 45,400 tonnes, <a href="/wiki/Kiev-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Kiev-class aircraft carrier">modified <i>Kiev</i> class</a>. The carrier was purchased by India on 20 January 2004 after years of negotiations at a final price of $2.35 billion. The ship successfully completed her sea trials in July 2013 and aviation trials in September 2013. She was formally commissioned on 16 November 2013 at a ceremony held at Severodvinsk, Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-ibnlive_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibnlive-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_2">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>India started the construction of a 40,000-tonne, 260-metre-long (850&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Vikrant-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Vikrant-class aircraft carrier"><i>Vikrant</i>-class</a> aircraft carrier in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-iac_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iac-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The new carrier will operate <a href="/wiki/MiG-29K" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-29K">MiG-29K</a> and naval <a href="/wiki/HAL_Tejas" title="HAL Tejas">HAL Tejas</a> aircraft along with the Indian-made helicopter <a href="/wiki/HAL_Dhruv" title="HAL Dhruv">HAL Dhruv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iac_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iac-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The ship will be powered by four gas-turbine engines and will have a range of 8,000 nautical miles (15,000 kilometres), carrying 160 officers, 1,400 sailors, and 40 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The carrier is being constructed by <a href="/wiki/Cochin_Shipyard" title="Cochin Shipyard">Cochin Shipyard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iac_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iac-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The ship was launched in August 2013 and is scheduled for commissioning in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-indiatoday.intoday.in_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indiatoday.intoday.in-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rss_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rss-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ndtv.com_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ndtv.com-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A second <i>Vikrant</i>-class carrier <a href="/wiki/INS_Vishal" title="INS Vishal">INS&#160;<i>Vishal</i></a> with a displacement of over 65,000 tons is planned and likely to be <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_marine_propulsion" title="Nuclear marine propulsion">nuclear-powered</a> with <a href="/wiki/CATOBAR" title="CATOBAR">CATOBAR</a> system to launch and recover heavier aircraft and <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_combat_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned combat aerial vehicle">unmanned combat aircraft</a>. The project is in the design phase as of April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cavour_(550).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Cavour_%28550%29.jpg/220px-Cavour_%28550%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cavour_(550).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/Italian_aircraft_carrier_Cavour_(550)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian aircraft carrier Cavour (550)"><i>Cavour</i></a> of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Navy" title="Italian Navy">Italian Navy</a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_7">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>2 STOVL carriers:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Italian_aircraft_carrier_Giuseppe_Garibaldi_(551)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian aircraft carrier Giuseppe Garibaldi (551)"><i>Giuseppe Garibaldi</i></a>: 14,000 tonne Italian STOVL carrier, commissioned in 1985.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Italian_aircraft_carrier_Cavour_(550)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian aircraft carrier Cavour (550)"><i>Cavour</i></a>: 27,000 tonne Italian STOVL carrier designed and built with secondary amphibious assault facilities, commissioned in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Helicopter_carrier_Hy%C5%ABga_(16DDH).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Helicopter_carrier_Hy%C5%ABga_(16DDH).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Helicopter carrier <i>Hy\xc5\xabga</i></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_8">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>4 helicopter carriers:\n</p>\n<ul><li>2 <a href="/wiki/Hy%C5%ABga-class_helicopter_destroyer" title="Hy\xc5\xabga-class helicopter destroyer"><i>Hy\xc5\xabga</i>-class&#x20;helicopter destroyers</a> \xe2\x80\x93 19,000 ton (full load) <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare_carrier" title="Anti-submarine warfare carrier">anti-submarine warfare carriers</a> with enhanced command-and-control capabilities allowing them to serve as fleet flagships.</li>\n<li>2 <a href="/wiki/Izumo-class_helicopter_destroyer" title="Izumo-class helicopter destroyer"><i>Izumo</i>-class&#x20;helicopter destroyer</a> \xe2\x80\x93 820-foot-long (250&#160;m), 19,500-ton (27,000 tons full load) <a href="/wiki/Helicopter_carrier" title="Helicopter carrier">helicopter carrier</a>, launched August 2013 and commissioned March 2015. This is the largest military ship Japan has had since World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-Indiastrategic.in_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indiastrategic.in-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><i>Izumo</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s sister ship, <i>Kaga</i>, was commissioned in 2017.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg/220px-Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg/330px-Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg/440px-Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1459" data-file-height="869" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Russian_aircraft_carrier_Kuznetsov.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Admiral_Kuznetsov" title="Russian aircraft carrier Admiral Kuznetsov">Russian aircraft carrier&#160;<i>Admiral Kuznetsov</i></a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_9">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>1 STOBAR carrier: <a href="/wiki/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Admiral_Kuznetsov" title="Russian aircraft carrier Admiral Kuznetsov"><i>Admiral Flota Sovetskovo Soyuza Kuznetsov</i></a>: 55,000 tonne <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Kuznetsov-class_aircraft_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiral Kuznetsov-class aircraft carrier"><i>Admiral Kuznetsov</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/STOBAR" title="STOBAR">STOBAR</a> aircraft carrier. Launched in 1985 as <i>Tbilisi</i>, renamed and operational from 1995. Without catapults she can launch and recover lightly fueled naval fighters for air defense or anti-ship missions but not heavy conventional bombing strikes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Officially designated an aircraft carrying cruiser, she is unique in carrying a heavy cruiser\'s complement of defensive weapons and large <a href="/wiki/P-700_Granit" title="P-700 Granit">P-700 Granit</a> offensive missiles. The P-700 systems will be removed in the coming refit to enlarge her below decks aviation facilities as well as upgrading her defensive systems.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_3">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Russian Government just recently gave the green light for the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Project_23000E" title="Project 23000E">Shtorm-class aircraft carrier</a>. This carrier will be a hybrid of CATOBAR and STOBAR, given the fact that she utilizes both systems of launching aircraft. The carrier is expected to cost between $1.8 billion and $5.63 billion. Once commissioned, she will replace <i>Admiral Kuznetsov</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit (LPH-6111)">ROKS&#160;<i>Dokdo</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Dokdo-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="Dokdo-class amphibious assault ship"><i>Dokdo</i>-class&#x20;amphibious assault ship</a> of the <a ship</a> 18,860 ton full deck amphibious assault ship with hospital and well deck and facilities to serve as fleet flagship.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_4">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>South Korea believes it can procure 2 light aircraft carriers by 2036, which will help make the ROKN a blue water navy.<sup href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_ship_Juan_Carlos_I_(L61)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish ship Juan Carlos I (L61)"><i>Juan Carlos I</i></a>: 27,000 tonne, specially designed multipurpose strategic projection ship which can operate as an <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">amphibious assault ship</a> and aircraft carrier. Juan Carlos I has full facilities for both functions including a <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_ski-jump" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft ski-jump">ski jump</a> for <a href="/wiki/STOVL" title="STOVL">STOVL</a> operations, is equipped with the <a href="/wiki/AV-8B_Harrier_II" class="mw-redirect" title="AV-8B Harrier II">AV-8B Harrier II</a> <a href="/wiki/Attack_aircraft" title="Attack aircraft">attack aircraft</a>. Also, <a href="/wiki/Well_deck" title="Well deck">well deck</a>, and vehicle storage area which can be used as additional hangar space, launched in 2008, commissioned 30 September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_5">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/TCG_Anadolu" title="TCG Anadolu">TCG <i>Anadolu</i> L-408</a> is a planned amphibious assault ship (LHD) of the Turkish Navy that can be configured as a light aircraft carrier. Construction began on 30 April 2016 by Sedef Shipbuilding Inc. at their Istanbul shipyard and is expected to be completed in 2021.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG/220px-DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG/330px-DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG/440px-DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="402" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/HTMS_Chakri_Naruebet" title="HTMS Chakri Naruebet">HTMS&#160;<i>Chakri Naruebet</i></a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Navy" title="Royal Thai Navy">Royal Thai Navy</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_12">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>One offshore helicopter support ship: <a href="/wiki/HTMS_Chakri_Naruebet" title="HTMS Chakri Naruebet">HTMS&#160;<i>Chakri Naruebet</i></a> helicopter carrier: 11,400 tonne STOVL carrier based on Spanish <a href="/wiki/Spanish_aircraft_carrier_Pr%C3%ADncipe_de_Asturias" title="Spanish aircraft carrier Pr\xc3\xadncipe de Asturias"><i>Pr\xc3\xadncipe de Asturias</i></a> design. Commissioned in 1997. The AV-8S Matador/Harrier STOVL fighter wing, mostly inoperable by 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> was retired from service without replacement in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Ship now used for royal transport, helicopter operations, and as a disaster relief platform.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_13">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>One STOVL carrier: the 65,000 tonne<sup id="cite_ref-HMSQE_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HMSQE-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)" title="HMS Queen Elizabeth (R08)">HMS&#160;<i>Queen Elizabeth</i></a> was commissioned in December 2017 with <a href="/wiki/Initial_operating_capability" title="Initial operating capability">Initial operating capability</a> scheduled for 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_6">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> is constructing the second of its larger STOVL <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> aircraft carriers, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Prince_of_Wales_(R09)" title="HMS Prince of Wales (R09)">HMS&#160;<i>Prince of Wales</i></a> to complete replacement of the three now retired <a href="/wiki/Invincible-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Invincible-class aircraft carrier"><i>Invincible</i>-class</a> carriers. <i>Prince of Wales</i> sailed for the first time in late 2017 and is expected to begin sea trials in 2019. <sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Each <i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class ship is able to operate around 40 aircraft during peace time operations, up to 50 during wartime, and will have a displacement of 65,000&#160;tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-HMSQE_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HMSQE-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pike_cvf_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pike_cvf-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_7486683_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org_7486683-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Wasp_(LHD_1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/USS_Wasp_%28LHD_1%29.jpg/220px-USS_Wasp_%28LHD_1%29.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="397" data-file-height="317" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Wasp_(LHD_1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amphibious assault ship <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(LHD-1)" title="USS Wasp (LHD-1)">USS&#160;<i>Wasp</i></a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_14">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>11 CATOBAR carriers, all nuclear-powered: \n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nimitz-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Nimitz-class aircraft carrier"><i>Nimitz</i>&#x20;class</a>: ten 101,000-ton, 1,092&#160;ft long fleet carriers, the first of which was commissioned in 1975. A <i>Nimitz</i>-class carrier is powered by two <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactors</a> providing steam to four <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">steam turbines</a> and is 1,092 feet (333&#160;m) long,</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Gerald R. Ford-class aircraft carrier"><i>Gerald R. Ford</i>&#x20;class</a>, one 110,000-ton, 1,106&#160;ft long fleet carrier. The lead of the class <a href="/wiki/USS_Gerald_R._Ford_(CVN-78)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Gerald R. Ford (CVN-78)"><i>Gerald R. Ford</i></a>, came into service in 2017, with another nine planned.</li></ul>\n<p>Nine amphibious assault ships carrying vehicles, Marine fighters, attack and transport helicopters, and landing craft with STOVL fighters for CAS and CAP:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/America-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="America-class amphibious assault ship"><i>America</i>&#x20;class</a>: a class of 45,000-ton amphibious assault ships, although the lead ship in this class does not have a well deck. One ship in service out of a planned 11 ships. Ships of this class can have a secondary mission as a light carrier with 20 <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_AV-8B_Harrier_II" title="McDonnell Douglas AV-8B Harrier II">AV-8B Harrier II</a>, and in the future the <a href="/wiki/F-35B_Lightning_II" class="mw-redirect" title="F-35B Lightning II">F-35B Lightning II</a> aircraft after unloading their Marine expeditionary unit.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wasp-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="Wasp-class amphibious assault ship"><i>Wasp</i>&#x20;class</a>: a class of eight 41,000-ton amphibious assault ships, members of this class have been used in wartime in their secondary mission as light carriers with 20 to 25 AV-8Bs after unloading their Marine expeditionary unit.</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_7">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Gerald_R._Ford_(CVN-78)_on_the_James_River_in_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/USS_Gerald_R._Ford_%28CVN-78%29_on_the_James_River_in_2013.JPG/330px-USS_Gerald_R._Ford_%28CVN-78%29_on_the_James_River_in_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/USS_Gerald_R._Ford_%28CVN-78%29_on_the_James_River_in_2013.JPG/440px-USS_Gerald_R._Ford_%28CVN-78%29_on_the_James_River_in_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3471" data-file-height="1044" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Gerald_R._Ford_(CVN-78)_on_the_James_River_in_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/USS_Gerald_R._Ford" title="USS Gerald R. Ford">USS&#160;<i>Gerald R. Ford</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Gerald R. Ford-class aircraft carrier"><i>Gerald R. Ford</i>-class&#x20;aircraft carrier</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The current US fleet of <i>Nimitz</i>-class carriers will be followed into service (and in some cases replaced) by the <a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Gerald R. Ford-class aircraft carrier"><i>Gerald R. Ford</i>&#x20;class</a>. It is expected that the ships will be more automated in an effort to reduce the amount of funding required to maintain and operate the vessels. The main new features are implementation of <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_Aircraft_Launch_System" title="Electromagnetic Aircraft Launch System">Electromagnetic Aircraft Launch System</a> (EMALS) (which replace the old steam catapults) and <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">unmanned aerial vehicles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Aircraft_Carriers_-_CVN_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aircraft_Carriers_-_CVN-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the deactivation of <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(CVN-65)" title="USS Enterprise (CVN-65)">USS&#160;<i>Enterprise</i></a> in December 2012, the U.S. fleet comprised 10 fleet carriers, but that number increased back to 11 with the commissioning of <i>Gerald R. Ford</i> in July 2017. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Armed_Services_Subcommittee_on_Seapower_and_Expeditionary_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="United States House Armed Services Subcommittee on Seapower and Expeditionary Forces">House Armed Services Seapower subcommittee</a> on 24 July 2007, recommended seven or eight new carriers (one every four years). However, the debate has deepened over budgeting for the $12\xe2\x80\x9314.5&#160;billion (plus $12&#160;billion for development and research) for the 100,000 ton <i>Gerald R. Ford</i>-class carrier (estimated service 2017) compared to the smaller $2&#160;billion 45,000 ton <a href="/wiki/America-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="America-class amphibious assault ship"><i>America</i>-class&#x20;amphibious assault ships</a>, which are able to deploy squadrons of F-35Bs. The first of this class, <a href="/wiki/USS_America_(LHA-6)" title="USS America (LHA-6)">USS&#160;<i>America</i></a>, is now in active service with another, <a href="/wiki/USS_Tripoli_(LHA-7)" title="USS Tripoli (LHA-7)">USS&#160;<i>Tripoli</i></a>, under construction and 9 more are planned.<sup id="cite_ref-AFAmag_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFAmag-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a report to Congress in February 2018, the Navy stated it intends to maintain a "12 <a href="/wiki/Hull_classification_symbol#Aircraft_carrier_type" title="Hull classification symbol">CVN</a> force" as part of its 30-year acquisition plan.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_carriers_in_preservation">Aircraft carriers in preservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Aircraft carriers in preservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_museum_carriers">Current museum carriers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Current museum carriers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A few aircraft carriers have been preserved as museum ships. They are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/USS_Yorktown_(CV-10)" title="USS Yorktown (CV-10)">USS&#160;<i>Yorktown</i>&#160;(CV-10)</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pleasant,_South_Carolina" title="Mount Pleasant, South Carolina">Mount Pleasant</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/USS_Intrepid_(CV-11)" title="USS Intrepid (CV-11)">USS&#160;<i>Intrepid</i>&#160;(CV-11)</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/USS_Hornet_(CV-12)" title="USS Hornet (CV-12)">USS&#160;<i>Hornet</i>&#160;(CV-12)</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alameda,_California" title="Alameda, California">Alameda</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/USS_Lexington_(CV-16)" title="USS Lexington (CV-16)">USS&#160;<i>Lexington</i>&#160;(CV-16)</a> in <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi,_Texas" title="Corpus Christi, Texas">Corpus Christi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/USS_Midway_(CV-41)" title="USS Midway (CV-41)">USS&#160;<i>Midway</i>&#160;(CV-41)</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Soviet_aircraft_carrier_Kiev" title="Soviet aircraft carrier Kiev">Soviet aircraft carrier&#160;<i>Kiev</i></a> in <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Soviet_aircraft_carrier_Minsk" title="Soviet aircraft carrier Minsk">Soviet aircraft carrier&#160;<i>Minsk</i></a> in <a href="/wiki/Nantong" title="Nantong">Nantong</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/INS_Viraat" title="INS Viraat">INS&#160;<i>Viraat</i></a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hermes_(R12)" title="HMS Hermes (R12)">HMS&#160;<i>Hermes</i>&#160;(R12)</a> will be preserved in <a href="/wiki/Kakinada" title="Kakinada">Kakinada</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_museum_carriers">Future museum carriers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aircraft_carrier&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Future museum carriers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/USS_Kitty_Hawk_(CV-63)" title="USS Kitty Hawk (CV-63)">USS&#160;<i>Kitty Hawk</i>&#160;(CV-63)</a> has a preservation campaign to bring her to <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Long Beach">Long Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. <i>Kitty Hawk</i> is to be kept in reserve until <a href="/wiki/USS_John_F._Kennedy_(CVN-79)" title="USS John F. Kennedy (CVN-79)">USS&#160;<i>John F. Kennedy</i>&#160;(CVN-79)</a> is commissioned in 2022.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/USS_John_F._Kennedy_(CV-67)" title="USS John F. Kennedy (CV-67)">USS&#160;<i>John F. Kennedy</i>&#160;(CV-67)</a> is the subject of a campaign for preservation at <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/USS_Tarawa_(LHA-1)" title="USS Tarawa (LHA-1)">USS&#160;<i>Tarawa</i>&#160;(LHA-1)</a> has a preservation campaign to bring her to the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast of the United States</a> as the world\'s first amphibious assault ship museum.</li></ul>\n<h2><span
